apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Beck';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"beck,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Beck
Hansen</b>
(born
<b>Bek
David
Campbell</b>,
July
8,
1970<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>),
known
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Stage_name?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stage
name">stage
name</a>
<b>Beck</b>,
is
an
<a
href="/wiki/United_States?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="United
States">American</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Musician?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Musician">musician</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Singer-songwriter?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Singer-songwriter">singer-songwriter</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Multi-instrumentalist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Multi-instrumentalist">multi-instrumentalist</a>.
Beck
rose
to
fame
in
the
early
1990s
with
his
<a
href="/wiki/Lo-fi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lo-fi"
class="mw-redirect">lo-fi</a>,
sonically
experimental
style,
and
he
became
well
known
for
creating
musical
<a
href="/wiki/Collage?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Collage">collages</a>
of
a
wide
range
of
styles.
His
later
recordings
encompass
<a
href="/wiki/Folk_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Folk
music">folk</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Funk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Funk">funk</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Soul_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soul
music">soul</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hip
hop
music">hip
hop</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative
rock">alternative
rock</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Country_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
music">country</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Psychedelic_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Psychedelic
music">psychedelia</a>.
Beck
has
released
ten
studio
albums,
as
well
as
several
non-album
singles
and
a
book
of
sheet
music.</p>








<p>Born
in
<a
href="/wiki/Los_Angeles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Los
Angeles">Los
Angeles</a>
in
1970,
Beck
discovered
hip
hop
and
folk
music
in
his
teens
and
began
to
perform
locally
at
coffeehouses
and
clubs.
He
moved
to
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
City">New
York
City</a>
in
1989
and
became
involved
in
the
city's
small
but
intense
<a
href="/wiki/Anti-folk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Anti-folk">anti-folk</a>
movement.
After
returning
to
his
hometown
in
the
early
1990s,
he
cut
his
breakthrough
<a
href="/wiki/Single_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Single
(music)">single</a>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Loser_(Beck_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Loser
(Beck
song)">Loser</a>&quot;,
which
became
a
worldwide
hit
in
1994.
His
1996
release
<i><a
href="/wiki/Odelay?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Odelay">Odelay</a></i>
produced
hit
singles,
topped
critic
polls
and
won
several
awards.
He
released
the
stripped-down
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mutations_(Beck_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mutations
(Beck
album)">Mutations</a></i>
in
1998,
and
the
funk-infused
<i><a
href="/wiki/Midnite_Vultures?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Midnite
Vultures">Midnite
Vultures</a></i>
in
1999.
The
downcast,
acoustic
<i><a
href="/wiki/Sea_Change_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sea
Change
(album)">Sea
Change</a></i>
(2002)
showcased
a
more
serious
Beck,
and
2005's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Guero?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guero">Guero</a></i>
returned
to
<a
href="/wiki/Sample_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sample
(music)"
class="mw-redirect">sample</a>-based
production.
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Information?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Information">The
Information</a></i>
(2006)
was
inspired
by
<a
href="/wiki/Hip_hop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hip
hop">hip
hop</a>,
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Modern_Guilt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Modern
Guilt">Modern
Guilt</a></i>
(2008),
likewise,
by
1960s
music.
In
February
2014,
Beck
released
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Morning_Phase?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Morning
Phase">Morning
Phase</a></i>.</p>








<p>With
a
<a
href="/wiki/Pop_art?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pop
art">pop
art</a>
collage
of
musical
styles,
oblique
and
<a
href="/wiki/Irony?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Irony">ironic</a>
lyrics,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Postmodern?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Postmodern"
class="mw-redirect">postmodern</a>
arrangements
incorporating
<a
href="/wiki/Sample_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sample
(music)"
class="mw-redirect">samples</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Drum_machine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drum
machine">drum
machines</a>,
live
instrumentation
and
sound
effects,
Beck
has
been
hailed
by
critics
and
the
public
throughout
his
musical
career
as
being
amongst
the
most
creative
and
idiosyncratic
musicians
of
1990s
and
2000s
<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative
rock">alternative
rock</a>.
Two
of
Beck's
most
popular
and
acclaimed
recordings
are
<i>Odelay</i>
and
<i>Sea
Change</i>,
both
of
which
were
ranked
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone
(magazine)"
class="mw-redirect">Rolling
Stone</a></i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
list
of
<a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone's
500
Greatest
Albums
of
All
Time">the
500
greatest
albums
of
all
time</a>.
The
four-time
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">platinum</a>
artist
has
collaborated
with
several
artists
and
has
made
several
contributions
to
soundtracks.
Beck
is
married
to
actress
<a
href="/wiki/Marissa_Ribisi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marissa
Ribisi">Marissa
Ribisi</a>,
and
is
a
<a
href="/wiki/Scientologist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scientologist"
class="mw-redirect">Scientologist</a>.</p>

style="overflow:hidden;height:;">

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_life">Early
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Beck&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
Early
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Beck
was
born
in
<a
href="/wiki/Los_Angeles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Los
Angeles">Los
Angeles</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="California">California</a>,
to
<a
href="/wiki/David_Campbell_(composer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Campbell
(composer)">David
Campbell</a>,
a
Canadian
musician,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Bibbe_Hansen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bibbe
Hansen">Bibbe
Hansen</a>,
a
visual
artist
and
former
<a
href="/wiki/Warhol_superstars?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warhol
superstars">Warhol
superstar</a>.
Bibbe's
maternal
grandmother
was
<a
href="/wiki/Jewish_people?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jewish
people"
class="mw-redirect">Jewish</a>,
while
Bibbe's
father,
<a
href="/wiki/Al_Hansen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Al
Hansen">Al
Hansen</a>,
was
partly
of
<a
href="/wiki/Norwegian_people?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Norwegian
people"
class="mw-redirect">Norwegian</a>
descent.<sup
id="cite_ref-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
mother
was
raised
amid
New
York's
<a
href="/wiki/The_Factory?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Factory">Andy
Warhol
Factory</a>
art
scene
of
the
1960s,<sup
id="cite_ref-rsencyclopedia_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rsencyclopedia-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
but
moved
to
California
at
age
17,
where
she
met
Campbell.<sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
father
is
a
Canadian-born
arranger,
composer
and
conductor
who
worked
on
hundreds
of
albums
and
numerous
films.<sup
id="cite_ref-rsencyclopedia_7-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rsencyclopedia-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Beck
began
life
in
a
rooming
house
near
downtown
Los
Angeles.
As
a
child,
he
lived
in
a
declining
neighborhood
just
off
<a
href="/wiki/Hollywood_Boulevard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hollywood
Boulevard">Hollywood
Boulevard</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs97_9-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs97-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;By
the
time
we
left
there,
they
were
ripping
out
miles
of
houses
en
masse
and
building
low-rent,
giant
apartment
blocks,&quot;
he
later
recalled.<sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
lower-class
family
struggled
financially,
moving
to
Hoover
and
Ninth
Street,
a
neighborhood
populated
primarily
by
<a
href="/wiki/Koreans?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Koreans">Koreans</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/El_Salvador?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="El
Salvador">Salvadorian</a>
refugees.<sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
was
sent
for
a
time
to
live
with
his
maternal
grandparents
in
<a
href="/wiki/Kansas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kansas">Kansas</a>,
with
Beck
later
remarking
that
&quot;I
think
they
were
kind
of
concerned&quot;
about
his
&quot;weird&quot;
home
life.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs94_10-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs94-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Since
his
paternal
grandfather
was
a
<a
href="/wiki/Presbyterianism?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Presbyterianism">Presbyterian</a>
minister,
Beck
grew
up
influenced
by
church
music
and
hymns.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs94_10-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs94-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
also
spent
time
in
Europe
with
his
maternal
grandfather,
<a
href="/wiki/Al_Hansen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Al
Hansen">Al
Hansen</a>,
a
visual
<a
href="/wiki/Collage?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Collage">collage</a>
artist
and
a
pioneer
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Avant-garde?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Fluxus?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fluxus">Fluxus</a>
movement.<sup
id="cite_ref-rsencyclopedia_7-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rsencyclopedia-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
his
parents
separated
when
he
was
ten,<sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
stayed
with
his
mother
and
brother
in
Los
Angeles,
where
he
was
influenced
by
the
city's
diverse
musical
offerings—everything
from
<a
href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hip
hop
music">hip
hop</a>
to
<a
href="/wiki/Latin_American_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Latin
American
music">Latin
music</a>
and
his
mother's
art
scene—all
of
which
would
later
reappear
in
his
recorded
and
published
work.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(August
2013)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
Beck
obtained
his
first
guitar
at
16
and
became
a
street
musician,
often
playing
<a
href="/wiki/Lead_Belly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lead
Belly">Lead
Belly</a>
covers
at
<a
href="/wiki/Lafayette_Park,_Los_Angeles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lafayette
Park,
Los
Angeles">Lafayette
Park</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs96_11-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs96-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
his
teens,
Beck
discovered
the
music
of
<a
href="/wiki/Sonic_Youth?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sonic
Youth">Sonic
Youth</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Pussy_Galore_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pussy
Galore
(band)">Pussy
Galore</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/X_(American_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="X
(American
band)">X</a>,
but
remained
uninterested
in
most
music
outside
folk
until
many
years
into
his
career.<sup
id="cite_ref-rsencyclopedia_7-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rsencyclopedia-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
contemporary
music
that
made
a
direct
connection
with
Beck
was
hip
hop,
which
he
first
heard
on
<a
href="/wiki/Grandmaster_Flash?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grandmaster
Flash">Grandmaster
Flash</a>
records
in
the
early
1980s.<sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
Growing
up
in
a
predominantly
<a
href="/wiki/Latin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Latin">Latin</a>
district,
he
found
himself
the
only
white
child
at
his
school,
and
he
quickly
learned
to
<a
href="/wiki/B-boying?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="B-boying">breakdance</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
When
he
was
17,
Beck
grew
fascinated
after
hearing
a
<a
href="/wiki/Mississippi_John_Hurt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mississippi
John
Hurt">Mississippi
John
Hurt</a>
record
at
a
friend's
house,<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
spent
hours
in
his
room
trying
to
emulate
the
<a
href="/wiki/Fingerstyle_guitar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fingerstyle
guitar">finger
picking</a>
of
the
country-blues
guitarist.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs94_10-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs94-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Shortly
thereafter,
Beck
explored
blues
and
folk
music
further,
discovering
<a
href="/wiki/Woody_Guthrie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Woody
Guthrie">Woody
Guthrie</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Blind_Willie_Johnson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blind
Willie
Johnson">Blind
Willie
Johnson</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Feeling
like
&quot;a
total
outcast&quot;,
Beck
dropped
out
of
school
after
junior
high.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
later
said
that
although
he
felt
school
was
important,
he
felt
unsafe
there.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs97_9-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs97-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
When
he
applied
to
the
new
<a
href="/wiki/Performing_arts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Performing
arts">performing
arts</a>
high
school
downtown,
he
was
rejected.<sup
id="cite_ref-nym12_13-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nym12-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
His
brother,
Channing,
took
him
to
post-<a
href="/wiki/Beat_Generation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Beat
Generation">Beat</a>
jazz
places
in
<a
href="/wiki/Echo_Park,_Los_Angeles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Echo
Park,
Los
Angeles">Echo
Park</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Silver_Lake,_Los_Angeles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Silver
Lake,
Los
Angeles">Silver
Lake</a>.
He
hung
out
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_City_College?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Los
Angeles
City
College">Los
Angeles
City
College</a>,
perusing
records,
books
and
old
<a
href="/wiki/Sheet_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sheet
music">sheet
music</a>
in
its
library.
He
used
a
fake
I.D.
to
sit
in
on
classes
there,
and
he
also
befriended
a
literature
instructor
and
his
poet
wife.<sup
id="cite_ref-nym12_13-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nym12-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
soon
began
a
stream
of
menial
jobs,
including
loading
trucks
and
operating
a
<a
href="/wiki/Leaf_blower?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Leaf
blower">leaf
blower</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Career">Career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Beck&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_performing_and_first_releases_.281985.E2.80.9393.29">Early
performing
and
first
releases
(1985–93)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Beck&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
Early
performing
and
first
releases
(1985–93)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Beck
began
as
a
<a
href="/wiki/Folk_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Folk
music">folk</a>
musician,
switching
between
<a
href="/wiki/Country_blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
blues">country
blues</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Delta_blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Delta
blues">Delta
blues</a>
and
more
traditional
rural
folk
music
in
his
teens.<sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
began
performing
on
city
buses,
often
covering
Mississippi
John
Hurt
alongside
original,
sometimes
improvisational
compositions.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs94_10-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs94-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;I'd
get
on
the
bus
and
start
playing
Mississippi
John
Hurt
with
totally
improvised
lyrics.
Some
drunk
would
start
yelling
at
me,
calling
me
<a
href="/wiki/Axl_Rose?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Axl
Rose">Axl
Rose</a>.
So
I'd
start
singing
about
Axl
Rose
and
the
levee
and
bus
passes
and
strychnine,
mixing
the
whole
thing
up,&quot;
he
later
recalled.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs94_10-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs94-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
was
also
in
a
band
called
Youthless
that
hosted
<a
href="/wiki/Dada?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dada">Dadaist</a>-inspired
freeform
events
at
city
coffee
shops.<sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;We
had
<a
href="/wiki/Radio_Shack?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radio
Shack"
class="mw-redirect">Radio
Shack</a>
mics
and
this
homemade
speaker
and
we'd
draft
people
in
the
audience
to
recite
comic
books
or
do
a
<a
href="/wiki/Beatbox?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Beatbox"
class="mw-redirect">beatbox</a>
thing,
or
we'd
tie
the
whole
audience
up
in
masking
tape,&quot;
Beck
recalled.<sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1989,
Beck
caught
a
bus
to
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
City">New
York
City</a>
with
little
more
than
eight
dollars
and
a
guitar.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs94_10-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs94-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
spent
the
summer
attempting
to
find
a
job
and
a
place
to
live
with
little
success.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs94_10-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs94-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
eventually
began
to
frequent
<a
href="/wiki/Manhattan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/Lower_East_Side?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lower
East
Side">Lower
East
Side</a>
and
stumbled
upon
the
tail
end
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/East_Village,_Manhattan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="East
Village,
Manhattan">East
Village</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/Anti-folk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Anti-folk">anti-folk</a>
scene's
first
wave.<sup
id="cite_ref-rsencyclopedia_7-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rsencyclopedia-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
became
involved
in
a
loose
posse
of
acoustic
musicians—including
<a
href="/wiki/Cindy_Lee_Berryhill?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cindy
Lee
Berryhill">Cindy
Lee
Berryhill</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Kirk_Kelly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kirk
Kelly">Kirk
Kelly</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Paleface_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paleface
(musician)">Paleface</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Lach_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lach
(musician)"
class="mw-redirect">Lach</a>,
headed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Manning?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Manning">Roger
Manning</a>—whose
raggedness
and
eccentricity
placed
them
well
outside
the
acoustic
mainstream.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-gp94_14-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gp94-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;The
whole
mission
was
to
destroy
all
the
clich&eacute;s
and
make
up
some
new
ones,&quot;
said
Beck
of
his
New
York
years.
&quot;Everybody
knew
each
other.
You
could
go
up
onstage
and
say
anything,
and
you
wouldn't
feel
weird
or
feel
any
pressure.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-gp94_14-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gp94-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
Inspired
by
that
freedom
and
by
the
local
spoken-word
performers,
Beck
began
to
write
free-associative,
<a
href="/wiki/Surrealism?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Surrealism">surrealistic</a>
songs
about
pizza,
<a
href="/wiki/MTV?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV">MTV</a>,
and
working
at
<a
href="/wiki/McDonald%27s?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a>,
turning
even
the
most
apparently
mundane
thoughts
into
songs.<sup
id="cite_ref-gp94_14-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gp94-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
was
roommates
with
<a
href="/wiki/Paleface_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paleface
(musician)">Paleface</a>,
sleeping
on
his
couch
and
attending
open
mic
nights
together.<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
Daunted
by
the
prospect
of
another
homeless
New
York
winter,
Beck
returned
to
his
home
of
Los
Angeles
in
early
1991.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;I
was
tired
of
being
cold,
tired
of
getting
beat
up,&quot;
he
later
remarked.
&quot;It
was
hard
to
be
in
New
York
with
no
money,
no
place[....]
I
kinda
used
up
all
the
friends
I
had.
Everyone
on
the
scene
got
sick
of
me.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-rs94_10-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs94-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Back
in
Los
Angeles,
Beck
began
to
work
at
a
video
store
in
<a
href="/wiki/Silver_Lake,_Los_Angeles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Silver
Lake,
Los
Angeles">Silver
Lake</a>
&quot;doing
things
like
alphabetizing
the
<a
href="/wiki/Pornography?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pornography">pornography</a>
section&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs94_10-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs94-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
began
performing
in
arty
Silver
Lake
clubs
and
coffeehouses—Al's
Bar,
<a
href="/wiki/Raji%27s?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Raji's">Raji's</a>
and
Jabberjaw—along
with
other
underground
acts
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Ethyl_Meatplow?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ethyl
Meatplow">Ethyl
Meatplow</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/That_Dog?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="That
Dog">That
Dog</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-rsencyclopedia_7-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rsencyclopedia-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-rs94_10-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs94-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
order
to
keep
indifferent
audiences
engaged
in
his
music,
Beck
would
play
in
a
spontaneous,
joking
manner.<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;I'd
be
banging
away
on
a
<a
href="/wiki/Son_House?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Son
House">Son
House</a>
tune
and
the
whole
audience
would
be
talking.
So
maybe
out
of
desperation
or
boredom,
or
the
audience's
boredom,
I'd
make
up
these
ridiculous
songs
just
to
see
if
people
were
listening,&quot;
he
later
remarked.<sup
id="cite_ref-ew97_18-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ew97-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
Virtually
an
unknown
to
the
public
and
an
enigma
to
those
who
met
him,
Beck
would
hop
onstage
between
acts
in
local
clubs
and
play
&quot;strange
folk
songs&quot;,
accompanied
by
&quot;what
could
best
be
described
as
<a
href="/wiki/Performance_art?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Performance
art">performance
art</a>&quot;
while
sometimes
wearing
a
<i><a
href="/wiki/Star_Wars?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Star
Wars">Star
Wars</a></i>
<a
href="/wiki/Stormtrooper_(Star_Wars)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stormtrooper
(Star
Wars)">stormtrooper</a>
mask.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
met
someone
who
offered
to
help
record
<a
href="/wiki/Demo_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Demo
(music)">demos</a>
in
his
living
room,
and
he
began
to
pass
<a
href="/wiki/Compact_Cassette?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Compact
Cassette">cassette
tapes</a>
around.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Eventually,
Beck
gained
key
boosters
in
Margaret
Mittleman,
the
West
Coast's
director
of
talent
acquisitions
for
<a
href="/wiki/BMG_Music_Publishing?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BMG
Music
Publishing"
class="mw-redirect">BMG
Music
Publishing</a>,
and
the
partners
behind
<a
href="/wiki/Independent_record_label?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Independent
record
label">independent
record
label</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Bong_Load_Custom_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bong
Load
Custom
Records">Bong
Load
Custom
Records</a>:
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Rothrock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Rothrock">Tom
Rothrock</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Rob_Schnapf?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rob
Schnapf">Rob
Schnapf</a>
and
Brad
Lambert.<sup
id="cite_ref-rsencyclopedia_7-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rsencyclopedia-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
Schnapf
saw
Beck
perform
at
Jabberjaw
and
felt
he
would
suit
their
small
venture.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
expressed
a
loose
interest
in
<a
href="/wiki/Hip_hop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hip
hop">hip
hop</a>,
and
Rothrock
introduced
him
to
Carl
Stephenson,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Record_producer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Record
producer">record
producer</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Rap-A-Lot_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rap-A-Lot
Records">Rap-A-Lot
Records</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1992,
Beck
visited
Stephenson's
home
to
collaborate.
The
result—the
<a
href="/wiki/Slide_guitar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Slide
guitar">slide</a>-<a
href="/wiki/Sampling_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sampling
(music)">sampling</a>
hip
hop
track
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Loser_(Beck_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Loser
(Beck
song)">Loser</a>&quot;—was
a
one-off
experiment
that
Beck
set
aside,
going
back
to
his
folk
songs,
making
his
home
tapes,
such
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Golden_Feelings?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Golden
Feelings">Golden
Feelings</a></i>,
and
releasing
several
independent
singles.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Mellow_Gold.2C_and_independent_albums_.281993.E2.80.9394.29"><i>Mellow
Gold</i>,
and
independent
albums
(1993–94)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Beck&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
Mellow
Gold,
and
independent
albums
(1993–94)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>By
1993,
Beck
was
living
in
a
rat-infested
shed
near
a
Los
Angeles
alleyway
with
little
money.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs94_10-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs94-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bong
Load
issued
&quot;Loser&quot;
as
a
single
in
March
1993
on
12&quot;
vinyl
with
only
500
copies
pressed.<sup
id="cite_ref-Palacios_77_20-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Palacios_77-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
felt
that
&quot;Loser&quot;
was
mediocre,
and
only
agreed
to
its
release
at
Rothrock's
insistence.<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Loser&quot;
unexpectedly
received
radio
airplay,
starting
in
Los
Angeles,
where
<a
href="/wiki/Campus_radio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Campus
radio">college
radio</a>
station
<a
href="/wiki/KXLU?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="KXLU">KXLU</a>
was
the
first
to
play
it,<sup
id="cite_ref-Palacios_77_20-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Palacios_77-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
later
on
<a
href="/wiki/Santa_Monica_College?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Santa
Monica
College">Santa
Monica
College</a>
radio
station
<a
href="/wiki/KCRW?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="KCRW">KCRW</a>,
where
radio
host
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Douridas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Douridas">Chris
Douridas</a>
played
the
song
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Morning_Becomes_Eclectic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Morning
Becomes
Eclectic">Morning
Becomes
Eclectic</a></i>,
the
station's
flagship
music
program.
&quot;I
called
the
record
label
that
day
and
asked
to
have
Beck
play
live
on
the
air,&quot;
Douridas
said.
&quot;He
came
in
that
Friday,
rapped
to
a
tape
of
'Loser'
and
did
his
song
'MTV
Makes
Me
Want
to
Smoke
Crack.'&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
That
night,
Beck
performed
at
the
Los
Angeles
club
Cafe
Troy
to
a
packed
audience
and
talent
scouts
from
major
labels.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
then
spread
to
Seattle
through
<a
href="/wiki/KNDD?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="KNDD">KNDD</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/KROQ-FM?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="KROQ-FM">KROQ-FM</a>
began
playing
the
song
on
an
almost
hourly
basis.<sup
id="cite_ref-Palacios_77_20-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Palacios_77-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
Bong
Load
struggled
to
press
more
copies
of
&quot;Loser&quot;,
Beck
was
beset
with
offers
to
sign
with
major
labels.<sup
id="cite_ref-Palacios_80_22-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Palacios_80-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
the
fierce
bidding
war
in
November,
Beck
spent
several
days
in
<a
href="/wiki/Olympia,_Washington?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Olympia,
Washington">Olympia,
Washington</a>,
recording
material
with
<a
href="/wiki/Calvin_Johnson_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Calvin
Johnson
(musician)">Calvin
Johnson</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Beat_Happening?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Beat
Happening">Beat
Happening</a>,
which
would
later
see
release
the
following
year
on
Johnson's
<a
href="/wiki/K_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="K
Records">K
Records</a>
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/One_Foot_in_the_Grave_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
Foot
in
the
Grave
(album)">One
Foot
in
the
Grave</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-bb93_23-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bb93-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>A
fierce
bidding
war
ensued,
with
<a
href="/wiki/Geffen_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Geffen
Records">Geffen
Records</a>
A&amp;R
director
Mark
Kates
signing
Beck
in
December
1993
despite
intense
competition
from
<a
href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warner
Bros.
Records">Warner
Bros.</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Capitol_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Capitol
Records">Capitol</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-bb93_23-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bb93-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck's
non-exclusive
contract
with
Geffen
allowed
him
an
unusual
amount
of
creative
freedom,
with
Beck
remaining
free
to
release
material
through
such
small,
independent
labels
as
<a
href="/wiki/Flipside_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Flipside
Records"
class="mw-redirect">Flipside</a>,
which
issued
the
sprawling,
25-track
collection
of
pre-&quot;Loser&quot;
recordings
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Stereopathetic_Soulmanure?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stereopathetic
Soulmanure">Stereopathetic
Soulmanure</a></i>
on
February
22
the
following
year.<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-bb93_23-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bb93-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
By
the
time
Beck
released
his
first
album
for
Geffen,
the
low-budget,
genre-blending
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mellow_Gold?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mellow
Gold">Mellow
Gold</a></i>
on
March
1,<sup
id="cite_ref-lat94_12-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lat94-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Loser&quot;
was
already
in
the
top
40
and
its
video
in
MTV's
<a
href="/wiki/Buzz_Bin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buzz
Bin">Buzz
Bin</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs97_9-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs97-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Loser&quot;
quickly
ascended
the
charts
in
the
US,
reaching
a
peak
of
number
ten
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100"><i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100</a>
singles
chart
and
topping
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_Modern_Rock_Tracks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
Modern
Rock
Tracks"
class="mw-redirect">Modern
Rock
Tracks</a>
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-US_charts_24-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-US_charts-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
also
charted
in
the
UK,
Australia,
New
Zealand,
and
throughout
Europe.
Beck's
newfound
position
of
attention
led
to
his
characterization
as
the
&quot;King
of
Slackers&quot;,
as
the
media
dubbed
him
the
center
of
the
new
so-called
&quot;slacker&quot;
movement.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
Critics,
feeling
it
the
essential
follow-up
to
<a
href="/wiki/Radiohead?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Creep_(Radiohead_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Creep
(Radiohead
song)">Creep</a>&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-bb93_23-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bb93-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
found
vacantness
in
the
lyrics
of
&quot;Loser&quot;
strongly
associated
with
<a
href="/wiki/Generation_X?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Generation
X">Generation
X</a>,
although
Beck
himself
strongly
contested
his
position
as
the
face
of
the
&quot;slacker&quot;
generation:
&quot;Slacker
my
<i>ass</i>.
I
mean,
I
<i>never</i>
had
any
slack.
I
was
working
a
$4-an-hour
job
trying
to
stay
alive.
That
slacker
stuff
is
for
people
who
have
the
time
to
be
depressed
about
everything.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-rs94_10-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs94-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Backlash_and_Odelay_.281994.E2.80.9397.29">Backlash
and
<i>Odelay</i>
(1994–97)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Beck&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
Backlash
and
Odelay
(1994–97)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Feeling
as
though
he
was
&quot;constantly
trying
to
prove
myself&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-rs97_9-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs97-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
suffered
a
backlash,
with
skeptics
denouncing
him
as
a
self-indulgent
fake
and
the
latest
marketing
opportunity.<sup
id="cite_ref-ew94_26-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ew94-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
summer
of
1994,
Beck
was
struggling
and
many
of
his
fellow
musicians
thought
he
had
lost
his
way.<sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
Combined
with
the
song's
wildly
popular
music
video
and
the
world
tour,
Beck
reacted
believing
the
attention
could
not
last,
resulting
in
a
status
as
a
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/One-hit_wonder?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One-hit
wonder">one-hit
wonder</a>&quot;.
At
other
concerts,
crowds
were
treated
to
twenty
minutes
of
<a
href="/wiki/Reggae?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reggae">reggae</a>
or
<a
href="/wiki/Miles_Davis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Miles
Davis">Miles
Davis</a>
or
<a
href="/wiki/Punk_jazz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Punk
jazz">jazz-punk</a>
iterations
of
&quot;Loser&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-nym12_13-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nym12-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
one-day
festivals
in
California,
he
surrounded
himself
with
an
artnoise
combo.
The
drummer
set
fire
to
his
cymbals;
the
lead
guitarist
&quot;played&quot;
his
char
with
the
strings
faced
towards
his
body;
and
Beck
changed
the
words
to
&quot;Loser&quot;
so
that
nobody
could
sing
along.<sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;I
can't
tell
you
how
many
times
I
was
looking
at
faces
that
were
looking
back
at
me
with
complete
bewilderment—or
just
pointing
and
shaking
their
heads
and
laughing—while
performing
during
that
period,&quot;
he
later
recalled.<sup
id="cite_ref-p4k11_27-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-p4k11-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
Despite
this,
Beck
gained
the
respect
of
his
peers,
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Petty?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Petty">Tom
Petty</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Johnny_Cash?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Johnny
Cash">Johnny
Cash</a>,
and
created
an
entire
wave
of
bands
determined
to
recapture
the
<i>Mellow
Gold</i>
sound.<sup
id="cite_ref-ocr96_28-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ocr96-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
Feeling
his
previous
releases
were
just
collections
of
demos
recorded
over
the
course
of
several
years,
Beck
desired
to
enter
the
studio
and
record
an
album
in
a
continuous
linear
fashion,
which
became
<i><a
href="/wiki/Odelay?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Odelay">Odelay</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-p4k11_27-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-p4k11-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Beck
blends
country,
blues,
rap,
jazz
and
rock
on
<i>Odelay</i>,
the
result
of
a
year
and
half
of
feverish
&quot;cutting,
pasting,
layering,
dubbing,
and,
of
course,
sampling&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs96_11-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs96-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
Each
day,
the
musicians
started
from
scratch,<sup
id="cite_ref-rs99_29-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs99-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
often
working
on
songs
for
16
hours
straight.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs96_11-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs96-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Odelay'</i>s
conception
lies
in
an
unfinished
studio
album
Beck
first
embarked
on
following
the
success
of
&quot;Loser&quot;,
chronicling
the
difficult
time
he
experienced:
&quot;There
was
a
cycle
of
everyone
dying
around
me,&quot;
he
recalled
later.<sup
id="cite_ref-ocr96_28-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ocr96-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
was
constantly
recording,
and
eventually
put
together
an
album
of
somber,
orchestrated
folk
tunes,
one
that,
perhaps,
&quot;could
have
been
a
commercial
blockbuster
along
with
similarly
themed
work
by
<a
href="/wiki/Smashing_Pumpkins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Smashing
Pumpkins"
class="mw-redirect">Smashing
Pumpkins</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Nine_Inch_Nails?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nine
Inch
Nails">Nine
Inch
Nails</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nirvana
(band)">Nirvana</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-ocr96_28-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ocr96-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
Instead,
Beck
plucked
one
song
from
it—the
<i>Odelay</i>
album
closer
&quot;Ramshackle&quot;—and
shelved
the
rest.<sup
id="cite_ref-q97_8-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-q97-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-ocr96_28-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ocr96-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
was
introduced
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Dust_Brothers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dust
Brothers">Dust
Brothers</a>,
producers
of
the
Beastie
Boys'
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Paul%27s_Boutique?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paul's
Boutique">Paul's
Boutique</a></i>,
whose
cut-and-paste,
sample-heavy
production
suited
Beck's
vision
of
a
more
fun,
accessible
album.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(August
2013)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
After
a
record
executive
explained
that
<i>Odelay</i>
would
be
a
&quot;huge
mistake&quot;,
he
spent
many
months
thinking
&quot;that
I'd
blown
it
forever&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-nym12_13-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nym12-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i>Odelay</i>
was
released
on
June
18,
1996,
to
commercial
success
and
critical
acclaim.
The
record
produced
several
hit
<a
href="/wiki/Single_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Single
(music)">singles</a>,
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Where_It%27s_At?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Where
It's
At">Where
It's
At</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Devils_Haircut_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Devils
Haircut
(song)"
class="mw-redirect">Devils
Haircut</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_New_Pollution?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
New
Pollution">The
New
Pollution</a>&quot;,
and
was
nominated
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Award</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Album
of
the
Year">Album
of
the
Year</a>
in
1997,
winning
a
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Award</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Alternative_Music_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Alternative
Music
Album">Best
Alternative
Music
Album</a>
as
well
as
a
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Male_Rock_Vocal_Performance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Male
Rock
Vocal
Performance">Grammy
Award
for
Best
Male
Rock
Vocal
Performance</a>
for
&quot;Where
It's
At&quot;.
During
one
busy
week
in
January
1997,
he
landed
his
Grammy
nominations,
appeared
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Saturday
Night
Live">Saturday
Night
Live</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Howard_Stern_(E!_show)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Howard
Stern
(E!
show)"
class="mw-redirect">Howard
Stern</a></i>,
and
did
a
last-minute
trot
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Rosie_O%27Donnell_Show?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Rosie
O'Donnell
Show">The
Rosie
O'Donnell
Show</a></i>.
The
combined
buzz
gave
<i>Odelay</i>
a
second
wind,
leading
to
an
expanded
fan
base
and
additional
exposure.<sup
id="cite_ref-ew97_18-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ew97-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
enjoyed
but,
like
several
executives
at
Geffen,
was
bewildered
by
the
success
of
<i>Odelay</i>.
He
would
often
get
recognized
in
public,
which
made
him
feel
strange.
&quot;It's
just
weird.
It
doesn't
feel
right.
It
doesn't
feel
natural
to
me.
I
don't
think
I
was
made
for
that.
I
was
never
good
at
that,&quot;
he
later
told
<a
href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pitchfork
Media">Pitchfork</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-p4k11_27-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-p4k11-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Odelay</i>
sold
two
million
copies
and
put
&quot;one-hit
wonder&quot;
criticisms
to
rest.
During
this
time,
he
contributed
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Deadweight_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Deadweight
(song)">Deadweight</a>&quot;
to
the
soundtrack
of
the
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/A_Life_Less_Ordinary?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Life
Less
Ordinary">A
Life
Less
Ordinary</a></i>
(1997).<sup
id="cite_ref-rs98_30-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs98-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Mutations_and_Midnite_Vultures_.281998.E2.80.932001.29"><i>Mutations</i>
and
<i>Midnite
Vultures</i>
(1998–2001)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Beck&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
Mutations
and
Midnite
Vultures
(1998–2001)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Having
not
been
in
a
proper
studio
since
&quot;Deadweight&quot;,
Beck
felt
anxious
to
&quot;go
in
and
just
do
some
stuff
real
quick&quot;,
and
compiled
several
songs
he
had
had
for
years.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs98_30-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs98-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
and
his
bandmates
hammered
out
fourteen
songs
in
fourteen
days,
although
just
twelve
made
it
onto
the
album,
1998's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mutations_(Beck_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mutations
(Beck
album)">Mutations</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs98_30-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs98-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
decided
on
<a
href="/wiki/Nigel_Godrich?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nigel
Godrich">Nigel
Godrich</a>,
producer
for
<a
href="/wiki/Radiohead?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/OK_Computer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="OK
Computer">OK
Computer</a></i>
the
previous
year,
to
be
behind
the
boards
for
the
project.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs98_30-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs98-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
Godrich
was
leaving
the
United
States
for
England
in
a
short
time,
which
led
to
the
album's
quick
production
schedule—&quot;No
looking
back,
no
doctoring
anything&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs98_30-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs98-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
whole
point
of
the
record
was
to
capture
the
performance
of
the
musicians
live,
an
uncharacteristic
far-cry
from
the
cut-and-paste
aesthetic
of
<i>Odelay</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs98_30-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs98-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
Though
the
album
was
originally
slated
for
release
by
Bong
Load
Records,
Geffen
intervened
and
issued
the
record
against
Beck's
wishes.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
artist
then
sought
to
void
his
contracts
with
both
record
labels,
and
in
turn
the
labels
sued
him
for
breach
of
contract.
The
litigation
went
on
for
years
and
it
remains
unclear
to
this
day
if
it
has
ever
been
completely
resolved.<sup
id="cite_ref-33"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
was
later
awarded
Best
Alternative
Music
Performance
for
<i>Mutations</i>
at
the
42nd
Grammy
Awards.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Midnite_Vultures?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Midnite
Vultures">Midnite
Vultures</a></i>,
Beck's
next
studio
effort,
was
originally
recorded
as
a
double
album,
and
more
than
25
nearly
completed
songs
were
left
behind.<sup
id="cite_ref-p4k11_27-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-p4k11-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
the
studio,
Beck
and
producers
studied
contemporary
hip
hop
and
R&amp;B,
specifically
<a
href="/wiki/R._Kelly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="R.
Kelly">R.
Kelly</a>,
in
order
to
embrace
and
incorporate
those
influences
in
the
way
<a
href="/wiki/Al_Green?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Al
Green">Al
Green</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Stax_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stax
Records">Stax</a>
records
had
done
in
previous
decades.<sup
id="cite_ref-p4k11_27-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-p4k11-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
July
1998,
a
core
group
began
to
assemble
at
Beck's
<a
href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pasadena,
California">Pasadena</a>
home:
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Justin_Meldal-Johnsen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Justin
Meldal-Johnsen">Justin
Meldal-Johnsen</a>,
keyboardist
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Joseph_Manning_Jr.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Joseph
Manning
Jr."
class="mw-redirect">Roger
Joseph
Manning
Jr.</a>,
and
producer-engineers
<a
href="/wiki/Mickey_Petralia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mickey
Petralia">Mickey
Petralia</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Tony_Hoffer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tony
Hoffer">Tony
Hoffer</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs99_29-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs99-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
Dozens
of
session
players
passed
through,
including
Beck's
father,
David
Campbell,
who
played
viola
and
arranged
some
of
the
strings.
The
musicians
held
communal
meals
and
mountain-bike
rides
on
dusty
trails
nearby,
but
remained
focused
on
Beck's
instructions:
to
make
an
up-tempo
album
that
would
be
fun
to
play
on
tour
night
after
night.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs99_29-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs99-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;I
had
so
many
things
going
on&quot;,
said
Beck
of
the
recording
process.
&quot;I
had
a
couple
of
rooms
of
computers
hooked
up,
I
was
doing
B
sides
for
Japan,
I
was
programming
beats
in
one
room
and
someone
would
be
cooking
dinner
in
the
other
room.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-rs99_29-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs99-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
November
1999,
Geffen
released
the
much-anticipated
<i>Midnite
Vultures</i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-35"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
which
attracted
confusion:
&quot;fans
and
critics
misguidedly
worried
whether
it
was
serious
or
a
goof,&quot;
and
as
a
result,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
New
York
Times">The
New
York
Times</a></i>
wrote
that
the
album
&quot;never
won
the
audience
it
deserved&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-nyt05_36-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nyt05-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
record
was
supported
by
an
extensive
world
tour.
For
Beck,
it
was
a
return
to
the
high-energy
performances
that
had
been
his
trademark
as
far
back
as
Lollapalooza.
The
live
stage
set
included
a
red
bed
that
descended
from
the
ceiling
for
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Debra_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Debra
(song)">Debra</a>&quot;,
and
the
touring
band
was
complemented
by
a
brass
section.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Midnite
Vultures</i>
was
nominated
for
Best
Album
at
the
43rd
Annual
Grammy
Awards.<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Sea_Change_.282002.E2.80.932003.29"><i>Sea
Change</i>
(2002–2003)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Beck&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
Sea
Change
(2002–2003)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
2000,
Beck
and
his
fianc&eacute;e,
stylist
Leigh
Limon,
ended
their
nine-year
relationship.<sup
id="cite_ref-age_39-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-age-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
lapsed
into
a
period
of
melancholy
and
introspection,
during
which
he
wrote
the
bleak,
acoustic-based
tracks
later
found
on
<i>Sea
Change</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-heartbreak_40-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-heartbreak-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
sat
on
the
songs,
not
wanting
to
talk
about
his
personal
life;
he
later
said
that
he
wanted
to
focus
on
music
and
&quot;not
really
strew
my
baggage
across
the
public
lobby&quot;.
Eventually,
however,
he
decided
the
songs
spoke
to
a
common
experience
(a
<a
href="/wiki/Relationship_breakup?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Relationship
breakup"
class="mw-redirect">relationship
breakup</a>),
and
that
it
would
not
seem
self-indulgent
to
record
them.<sup
id="cite_ref-beckchecksin_41-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-beckchecksin-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2001,
Beck
drifted
back
to
the
songs
and
called
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Nigel_Godrich?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nigel
Godrich">Nigel
Godrich</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-time_42-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-time-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Retailers
initially
predicted
that
the
album
would
not
receive
much
radio
support,
but
they
also
believed
that
Beck's
maverick
reputation
and
critical
acclaim,
in
addition
to
the
possibility
of
multiple
Grammy
nominations,
might
offset
<i>Sea
Change'</i>s
uncommercial
sound.<sup
id="cite_ref-beckchecksin_41-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-beckchecksin-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Sea
Change</i>,
issued
by
Geffen
in
September
2002,
was
regardless
a
commercial
hit
and
critical
darling,<sup
id="cite_ref-nyt05_36-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nyt05-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
revering
it
as
&quot;the
best
album
Beck
has
ever
made,
[...]
an
impeccable
album
of
truth
and
light
from
the
end
of
love.
This
is
his
<i><a
href="/wiki/Blood_on_the_Tracks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blood
on
the
Tracks">Blood
on
the
Tracks</a></i>.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-rs02review_43-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs02review-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
later
listed
by
the
magazine
as
one
of
the
best
records
of
the
decade
and
of
all-time,
and
it
also
placed
second
on
the
year's
<a
href="/wiki/Pazz_%26_Jop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pazz
&amp;
Jop">Pazz
&amp;
Jop</a>
Critics
Poll.
<i>Sea
Change</i>
yielded
a
low-key,
theater-based
acoustic
tour,
as
well
as
a
larger
tour
with
<a
href="/wiki/The_Flaming_Lips?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Flaming
Lips">The
Flaming
Lips</a>
as
Beck's
opening
and
backing
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-becktour_44-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-becktour-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-flaminglips_45-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-flaminglips-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck
was
playful
and
energetic,
sometimes
throwing
in
covers
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Rolling
Stones">The
Rolling
Stones</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Big_Star?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Big
Star">Big
Star</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Zombies?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Zombies">The
Zombies</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Velvet_Underground?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Velvet
Underground">The
Velvet
Underground</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-rs02review_43-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rs02review-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-jackwhite_46-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-jackwhite-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Following
the
release
of
<i>Sea
Change</i>,
Beck
felt
newer
compositions
were
sketches
for
something
more
evolved
in
the
same
direction,
and
wrote
nearly
35
more
songs
in
the
coming
months,
keeping
demos
of
them
on
tapes
in
a
suitcase.<sup
id="cite_ref-p4k11_27-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-p4k11-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
his
solo
tour,
the
tapes
were
left
backstage
during
a
stop
in
Washington,
D.C.,
and
Beck
was
never
able
to
recover
them.
It
was
disheartening
to
the
musician,
who
felt
the
two
years
of
songwriting
represented
something
more
technically
complex.
As
a
result,
Beck
took
a
break
and
wrote
no
original
compositions
in
2003.<sup
id="cite_ref-p4k11_27-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-p4k11-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
Feeling
as
though
it
might
take
him
a
while
to
&quot;get
back
to
that
[songwriting]
territory&quot;,
he
entered
the
studio
with
Dust
Brothers
to
complete
a
project
that
dated
back
to
<i>Odelay</i>.
Nearly
half
of
the
songs
had
existed
since
the
1990s.<sup
id="cite_ref-p4k11_27-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-p4k11-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Guero_and_The_Information_.282004.E2.80.932007.29"><i>Guero</i>
and
<i>The
Information</i>
(2004–2007)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Beck&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
Guero
and
The
Information
(2004–2007)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Guero?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guero">Guero</a></i>,
Beck's
eighth
studio
album,
was
recorded
over
the
span
of
nine
months
during
which
several
significant
events
occurred
in
his
life:
his
girlfriend,
Marissa
Ribisi,
became
pregnant;
they
were
married;
their
son,
Cosimo,
was
born;
and
they
moved
out
of
Silver
Lake.<sup
id="cite_ref-nyt05_36-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nyt05-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-guerolito_47-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-guerolito-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
collaboration
with
the
Dust
Brothers,
his
second,
was
notable
for
their
use
of
high-tech
measures
to
achieve
a
low-fi
sound.<sup
id="cite_ref-nyt05_36-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nyt05-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
For
example,
after
recording
a
&quot;sonically
perfect&quot;
version
of
a
song
at
one
of
the
nicest
recording
studios
in
Hollywood,
the
Dust
Brothers
processed
it
in
an
<a
href="/wiki/Echoplex?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Echoplex">Echoplex</a>
to
create
a
gritty,
reverb-heavy
sound:
&quot;We
did
this
high-tech
recording
and
ran
it
through
a
<a
href="/wiki/Transistor_radio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Transistor
radio">transistor
radio</a>.
It
sounded
too
good,
that
was
the
problem.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-nyt05_36-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nyt05-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
Initially
due
to
be
released
in
October
2004,
<i>Guero</i>
faced
delays
and
did
not
come
out
till
March
2005,
though
unmastered
copies
of
the
tracks
surfaced
online
in
January.<sup
id="cite_ref-finished_48-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-finished-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i>Guero</i>
debuted
at
number
two
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>,
selling
162,000
copies,
an
all-time
sales
high.<sup
id="cite_ref-guerobb_49-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-guerobb-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>
Lead
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/E-Pro?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="E-Pro">E-Pro</a>&quot;
peaked
at
number
one
at
Modern
Rock
radio,
making
it
his
first
chart-topper
since
&quot;Loser&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-charts_50-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-charts-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
Beck,
inspired
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Nintendocore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nintendocore">Nintendocore</a>
remix
scene
and
feeling
a
connection
with
its
lo-fi,
home-recording
method,
collaborated
with
artists
<a
href="/wiki/8-bit_(band)?qsrc=3044"
